I still haven't read the right feature about the difficulties in tracking podcast traffic and how it's like the Wild Wild West even now in 2018 with all the money that's flowing in... even Apple's podcast rankings are flawed and pretty easy to exploit if you want to cheat.
There still isn't a foolproof way to measure podcast traffic. The closest is probably Apple's episode charts, which measures total downloads within 24 hours of a new episode posting, but even then - Apple usually generates 60-70% of someone's podcast traffic and that's it.
To get tracked by Podtrac, you have to sign up with them, then redirect your RSS feed to them so they can track the traffic. We didn't do this for a variety of reasons. Neither does any podcast that uses @midrollmedia for ad sales.
In this podcast boom piece, the writer relies on Podtrac for download info/rankings/conclusions but never mentions that The @Ringer + many other pods do NOT allow Podtrac to track their data. Only pods that sign up with Podtrac get "ranked" by them.   https://t.co/q8mIg8CjpY
